This issue was previously reported in #27419 and partially addressed, but the root cause — `onReplyStart` unconditionally resetting the typing breaker on every streaming chunk (`typing.ts:71-85`) — was not fixed, causing the problem to persist in later versions (confirmed on 2026.3.12+ with proxy configurations). The result is a cascade: streaming chunks repeatedly reset the typing circuit breaker, flooding the network with failing `sendChatAction` requests for 30s+, while the polling stall watchdog takes 90s to detect the outage. Meanwhile, outbound `sendMessage`/`editMessageText` calls fail silently with no retry.\\n- **Why it matters:** Users behind proxies lose AI replies entirely during transient network disruptions.\\n- **What changed:**\\n  1. **Typing guard semantics** — `onReplyStart` now only resets the breaker on the first call per reply cycle; subsequent streaming chunks refresh the TTL but never restart an already-tripped breaker\\n  2. **Outbound network health signal** — `sendChatAction` handler tracks consecutive recoverable network failures and triggers early polling restart (instead of waiting 90s)\\n  3. **Pre-connect send retry** — final replies, preview edits, text fallbacks, and user-visible error messages all retry on safe pre-connect network errors (connection refused, DNS, socket hang up) with exponential backoff\\n  4. **Configurable stall threshold** — new optional `channels.telegram.network.pollStallThresholdMs` lets proxy users lower the watchdog from the 90s default\\n  5. **Watchdog false positive fix** — polling stall detection now checks `runner.size()` to avoid false restarts when updates are still being processed (backpressure)\\n- **What did NOT change (scope boundary):** No transport fallback bypass for explicit proxies — respects user network policy. No changes to `reply-dispatcher.ts` error handling or general retry infrastructure.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [x] Integrations\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #27419\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n- Typing indicator no longer spams failing requests during network outages (was: 30s+ of error log flooding)\\n- Telegram replies now retry on safe pre-connect network errors instead of silently failing\\n- Polling recovery is faster when outbound sends detect network failure (seconds vs 90s)\\n- New optional config: `channels.telegram.network.pollStallThresholdMs` (default: 90000)\\n\\n## Security Impact (required)\\n\\n- New permissions/capabilities? Log transports registered by the diagnostics-otel plugin silently never attach to the real logger, so no OTLP log records are emitted. This PR moves the transport registry and the active logger reference to a `globalThis.__openclawLogTransportState` singleton, mirroring the existing pattern used by `__openclawDiagnosticEventsState` in `diagnostic-events.ts`.\\n\\n2. **Add opt-in content capture for OTEL traces** — Adds a `diagnostics.otel.includeContent` config flag (default: `false`) that gates attaching user-facing input/output text to `model.usage` trace spans. When enabled, content is emitted as standard `gen_ai.prompt` / `gen_ai.completion` attributes (primary), with `langfuse.observation.input` / `langfuse.observation.output` as secondary compatibility fields. All content is redacted via `redactSensitiveText` before export.\\n\\n## Why one PR\\n\\nThese are two independent fixes that happen to be small enough to review together (+86/-6 across 8 files). Shipping them separately is also fine — the log transport fix has no dependency on content capture, and vice versa.\\n\\n## Relation to existing PRs and issues\\n\\n### Issues addressed\\n\\n- **#39156** — diagnostics-otel plugin: OTLP log export doesn\\u0026#39;t work — module isolation between gateway and plugin-sdk\\n- **#44943** — `diagnostics.otel: Unrecognized key: \\u0026#34;captureContent\\u0026#34;` — this PR adds `includeContent` to the strict Zod schema so the config key is accepted\\n- **#45096** — v3.12 diagnostics-otel plugin only reports system metrics, no LLM call traces/spans — this PR adds `gen_ai.*` semantic convention attributes to `model.usage` spans\\n\\n### Improvements over existing PRs\\n\\n**Log transport fix — compared with #50085, #39163, #24258:**\\n\\nThis PR takes the same approach as #50085 (the strongest of the three) by sharing **both** the transport registry **and** the active logger reference via `globalThis`. PRs #39163 and #24258 only share the `externalTransports` Set but not the logger reference, which leaves the late-registration path broken: if the daemon\\u0026#39;s logger is already built before the plugin calls `registerLogTransport`, the transport still needs to be attached to the live logger immediately. Without a shared `activeLogger`, `registerLogTransport` reads `loggingState.cachedLogger` which is `null` in the plugin\\u0026#39;s module instance, so the transport silently never attaches.\\n\\n**Content capture — compared with #36231, #21290, #40254:**\\n\\n- Smaller and more focused than #21290 (5735 lines, 40 files) — this PR takes the incremental approach of extending the existing `model.usage` flow rather than redesigning the span hierarchy\\n- Uses standard `gen_ai.*` attributes as the primary content fields (unlike #36231 which uses Langfuse-specific attrs as primary)\\n- Includes Langfuse compatibility attrs as secondary fields (unlike #21290 which only uses standard attrs)\\n- Does not include unrelated files like `PATCHES.md` (present in #36231)\\n- Covers the same emission site as #36231 (`agent-runner.ts`) with the same gating approach (`cfg.diagnostics?.otel?.includeContent`)\\n\\n### Scope note\\n\\nContent capture in this PR is at the reply layer (`agent-runner.ts`), capturing user-facing input/output text — not raw provider request/response bodies, reasoning internals, or tool call content. This is the only `model.usage` emitter in the current codebase. If other emitters are added, they will need the same `includeContent` gate.\\n\\n## Files changed (8)\\n\\n| File | Change |\\n|---|---|\\n| `src/logging/logger.ts` | `globalThis` singleton for This issue was previously reported in #27419 and partially addressed, but the root cause — `onReplyStart` unconditionally resetting the typing breaker on every streaming chunk (`typing.ts:71-85`) — was not fixed, causing the problem to persist in later versions (confirmed on 2026.3.12+ with proxy configurations). The result is a cascade: streaming chunks repeatedly reset the typing circuit breaker, flooding the network with failing `sendChatAction` requests for 30s+, while the polling stall watchdog takes 90s to detect the outage. Meanwhile, outbound `sendMessage`/`editMessageText` calls fail silently with no retry.\\n- **Why it matters:** Users behind proxies lose AI replies entirely during transient network disruptions.\\n- **What changed:**\\n  1. **Typing guard semantics** — `onReplyStart` now only resets the breaker on the first call per reply cycle; subsequent streaming chunks refresh the TTL but never restart an already-tripped breaker\\n  2. **Outbound network health signal** — `sendChatAction` handler tracks consecutive recoverable network failures and triggers early polling restart (instead of waiting 90s)\\n  3. **Pre-connect send retry** — final replies, preview edits, text fallbacks, and user-visible error messages all retry on safe pre-connect network errors (connection refused, DNS, socket hang up) with exponential backoff\\n  4. **Configurable stall threshold** — new optional `channels.telegram.network.pollStallThresholdMs` lets proxy users lower the watchdog from the 90s default\\n  5. **Watchdog false positive fix** — polling stall detection now checks `runner.size()` to avoid false restarts when updates are still being processed (backpressure)\\n- **What did NOT change (scope boundary):** No transport fallback bypass for explicit proxies — respects user network policy. No changes to `reply-dispatcher.ts` error handling or general retry infrastructure.\\n\\n## Change Type (select all)\\n\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n\\n## Scope (select all touched areas)\\n\\n- [x] Integrations\\n\\n## Linked Issue/PR\\n\\n- Closes #27419\\n\\n## User-visible / Behavior Changes\\n\\n- Typing indicator no longer spams failing requests during network outages (was: 30s+ of error log flooding)\\n- Telegram replies now retry on safe pre-connect network errors instead of silently failing\\n- Polling recovery is faster when outbound sends detect network failure (seconds vs 90s)\\n- New optional config: `channels.telegram.network.pollStallThresholdMs` (default: 90000)\\n\\n## Security Impact (required)\\n\\n- New permissions/capabilities? No\\n- Secrets/tokens handling changed? No\\n- New/changed network calls? No (existing calls gain retry on pre-connect errors only)\\n- Command/tool execution surface changed? No\\n- Data access scope changed? When compaction aborts and retries, the counter increments but the session context stays the same, causing the same content to be flushed repeatedly (4-7x duplicate entries reported).\\n\\nRoot cause: `compactionCount` conflates \\u0026#34;compaction cycle count\\u0026#34; with \\u0026#34;content has changed\\u0026#34; — these are independent concerns. Two different compaction cycles can see identical context (abort → retry scenario), so event-based dedup is fundamentally wrong for this use case.\\n\\n## How\\n- **State-based dedup**: compute a SHA-256 hash (truncated to 16 hex chars) of `messages.length + last 3 user/assistant message contents` before each flush. If the hash matches the stored `memoryFlushContextHash`, skip the flush.\\n- **Two-layer design**: `shouldRunMemoryFlush()` unchanged (token threshold gate), hash check added as second gate in `runMemoryFlushIfNeeded()`.\\n- **`willRetry` fix**: `onAgentEvent` now checks `!evt.data?.willRetry` before marking `memoryCompactionCompleted = true`, preventing retry-in-progress compaction from being incorrectly treated as completed.\\n- **Performance**: `readTranscriptTailMessages()` reads only the last 64KB of the transcript file (not the full file).\\n- **Hash timing**: stores the hash computed *before* the flush run (not after), since the flush turn itself writes to the transcript and would change the hash.\\n\\n### Scenario behavior\\n| Scenario | Behavior |\\n|----------|----------|\\n| Compaction abort | messages unchanged → hash unchanged → skip ✅ |\\n| Compaction success | messages compressed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| New messages | tail content changed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| Persistence failure | `contextHashBeforeFlush` used in-memory → no re-flush within session ✅ |\\n\\n## Files changed (3 + 1 test)\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.ts` — new `computeContextHash()` function\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/agent-runner-memory.ts` — hash check gate + willRetry fix + tail reader\\n- `src/config/sessions/types.ts` — add `memoryFlushContextHash` field to `SessionEntry`\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.test.ts` — 8 unit tests for `computeContextHash`\\n\\n## Testing\\n- [x] On every subsequent request `resolveSessionModelRef` would return the fallback model, so the configured primary was **never retried** after it recovered.\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\n`updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun` unconditionally calls `setSessionRuntimeModel(next, { provider: providerUsed, model: modelUsed })` after every run. When a fallback ran, `providerUsed`/`modelUsed` reflect the fallback, and this gets written to `entry.model` / `entry.modelProvider`. `resolveSessionModelRef` then returns the stored runtime model on every future call, bypassing the configured primary entirely.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nAdd an `isFromFallback` parameter to `updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun`. When true, skip `setSessionRuntimeModel` so the session entry retains no runtime model (or retains its previous primary if one was stored). On the next request the session has no stale fallback recorded, so `resolveSessionModelRef` returns the configured primary and it gets a fresh retry.\\n\\nThe same guard is applied in the cron/isolated-agent path, which calls `setSessionRuntimeModel` directly.\\n\\nThe `isFromFallback` flag is computed at the agent.ts callsite as:\\n```ts\\nisFromFallback: fallbackModel !== model || fallbackProvider !== provider\\n```\\n\\n## What this does NOT change\\n\\n- Context token tracking still uses the actual model that ran (correct for prompt sizing)\\n- CLI session ID recording is unaffected\\n- The fallback model is still used for the current run — only the persistence step is skipped\\n- No change to `resolveSessionModelRef` itself\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\nExisting unit tests pass. Tools now describe what they produced (`details.media`) instead of declaring delivery instructions (`details.reply`). Media is collected during tool execution and attached to the assistant reply through the block reply pipeline, replacing the immediate `onToolResult` delivery path.\\n\\n### Changes\\n\\n**`details.reply` renamed to `details.media`**: tools report produced artifacts, not delivery instructions. When compaction aborts and retries, the counter increments but the session context stays the same, causing the same content to be flushed repeatedly (4-7x duplicate entries reported).\\n\\nRoot cause: `compactionCount` conflates \\u0026#34;compaction cycle count\\u0026#34; with \\u0026#34;content has changed\\u0026#34; — these are independent concerns. Two different compaction cycles can see identical context (abort → retry scenario), so event-based dedup is fundamentally wrong for this use case.\\n\\n## How\\n- **State-based dedup**: compute a SHA-256 hash (truncated to 16 hex chars) of `messages.length + last 3 user/assistant message contents` before each flush. If the hash matches the stored `memoryFlushContextHash`, skip the flush.\\n- **Two-layer design**: `shouldRunMemoryFlush()` unchanged (token threshold gate), hash check added as second gate in `runMemoryFlushIfNeeded()`.\\n- **`willRetry` fix**: `onAgentEvent` now checks `!evt.data?.willRetry` before marking `memoryCompactionCompleted = true`, preventing retry-in-progress compaction from being incorrectly treated as completed.\\n- **Performance**: `readTranscriptTailMessages()` reads only the last 64KB of the transcript file (not the full file).\\n- **Hash timing**: stores the hash computed *before* the flush run (not after), since the flush turn itself writes to the transcript and would change the hash.\\n\\n### Scenario behavior\\n| Scenario | Behavior |\\n|----------|----------|\\n| Compaction abort | messages unchanged → hash unchanged → skip ✅ |\\n| Compaction success | messages compressed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| New messages | tail content changed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| Persistence failure | `contextHashBeforeFlush` used in-memory → no re-flush within session ✅ |\\n\\n## Files changed (3 + 1 test)\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.ts` — new `computeContextHash()` function\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/agent-runner-memory.ts` — hash check gate + willRetry fix + tail reader\\n- `src/config/sessions/types.ts` — add `memoryFlushContextHash` field to `SessionEntry`\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.test.ts` — 8 unit tests for `computeContextHash`\\n\\n## Testing\\n- [x] `pnpm build` passes\\n- [x] `pnpm check` passes (lint + format)\\n- [x] `pnpm test` — 811/812 pass (1 pre-existing failure in `process-respawn.test.ts`)\\n- [x] 8 new unit tests for `computeContextHash` (empty input, object content, undefined content, system message filtering, length differentiation, tail behavior)\\n- [x] AI-assisted (OpenClaw agents 李飞飞/陈皮皮/毛豆豆, cross-reviewed, fully tested)\\n\\n## Backward compatibility\\n- `memoryFlushContextHash` undefined → falls back to existing `compactionCount` logic\\n- `memoryFlushCompactionCount` field preserved (not removed)\\n- The lobster way. 🦞 \"}},\"created_at\":\"2026-03-21T18:44:59Z\",\"updated_at\":\"2026-03-21T18:45:12Z\"},{\"number\":48417,\"title\":\"fix(agent): do not persist fallback model as session runtime model\",\"body\":\"## Summary\\n\\nFixes #47705.\\n\\nWhen the primary model is temporarily unavailable (overloaded, rate-limited) and a fallback handles the request, the fallback model was being written back to the session store via `setSessionRuntimeModel`. On every subsequent request `resolveSessionModelRef` would return the fallback model, so the configured primary was **never retried** after it recovered.\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\n`updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun` unconditionally calls `setSessionRuntimeModel(next, { provider: providerUsed, model: modelUsed })` after every run. When a fallback ran, `providerUsed`/`modelUsed` reflect the fallback, and this gets written to `entry.model` / `entry.modelProvider`. `resolveSessionModelRef` then returns the stored runtime model on every future call, bypassing the configured primary entirely.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nAdd an `isFromFallback` parameter to `updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun`. When true, skip `setSessionRuntimeModel` so the session entry retains no runtime model (or retains its previous primary if one was stored). On the next request the session has no stale fallback recorded, so `resolveSessionModelRef` returns the configured primary and it gets a fresh retry.\\n\\nThe same guard is applied in the cron/isolated-agent path, which calls `setSessionRuntimeModel` directly.\\n\\nThe `isFromFallback` flag is computed at the agent.ts callsite as:\\n```ts\\nisFromFallback: fallbackModel !== model || fallbackProvider !== provider\\n```\\n\\n## What this does NOT change\\n\\n- Context token tracking still uses the actual model that ran (correct for prompt sizing)\\n- CLI session ID recording is unaffected\\n- The fallback model is still used for the current run — only the persistence step is skipped\\n- No change to `resolveSessionModelRef` itself\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\nExisting unit tests pass. The fix is covered by the existing `session-store.test.ts` and `run.cron-model-override.test.ts` suites (38 tests across 9 files, all green).\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/48417\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"amittell\",\"id\":1388680,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/amittell\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/1388680?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"commands\",\"agents\",\"size: M\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"fix/47705-fallback-model-no-persist\",\"sha\":\"7bc6f9702b2856b52c139b3fee26657b18472b48\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"amittell/openclaw\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant. Any OS. Any Platform. When compaction aborts and retries, the counter increments but the session context stays the same, causing the same content to be flushed repeatedly (4-7x duplicate entries reported).\\n\\nRoot cause: `compactionCount` conflates \\u0026#34;compaction cycle count\\u0026#34; with \\u0026#34;content has changed\\u0026#34; — these are independent concerns. Two different compaction cycles can see identical context (abort → retry scenario), so event-based dedup is fundamentally wrong for this use case.\\n\\n## How\\n- **State-based dedup**: compute a SHA-256 hash (truncated to 16 hex chars) of `messages.length + last 3 user/assistant message contents` before each flush. If the hash matches the stored `memoryFlushContextHash`, skip the flush.\\n- **Two-layer design**: `shouldRunMemoryFlush()` unchanged (token threshold gate), hash check added as second gate in `runMemoryFlushIfNeeded()`.\\n- **`willRetry` fix**: `onAgentEvent` now checks `!evt.data?.willRetry` before marking `memoryCompactionCompleted = true`, preventing retry-in-progress compaction from being incorrectly treated as completed.\\n- **Performance**: `readTranscriptTailMessages()` reads only the last 64KB of the transcript file (not the full file).\\n- **Hash timing**: stores the hash computed *before* the flush run (not after), since the flush turn itself writes to the transcript and would change the hash.\\n\\n### Scenario behavior\\n| Scenario | Behavior |\\n|----------|----------|\\n| Compaction abort | messages unchanged → hash unchanged → skip ✅ |\\n| Compaction success | messages compressed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| New messages | tail content changed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| Persistence failure | `contextHashBeforeFlush` used in-memory → no re-flush within session ✅ |\\n\\n## Files changed (3 + 1 test)\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.ts` — new `computeContextHash()` function\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/agent-runner-memory.ts` — hash check gate + willRetry fix + tail reader\\n- `src/config/sessions/types.ts` — add `memoryFlushContextHash` field to `SessionEntry`\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.test.ts` — 8 unit tests for `computeContextHash`\\n\\n## Testing\\n- [x] `pnpm build` passes\\n- [x] `pnpm check` passes (lint + format)\\n- [x] `pnpm test` — 811/812 pass (1 pre-existing failure in `process-respawn.test.ts`)\\n- [x] 8 new unit tests for `computeContextHash` (empty input, object content, undefined content, system message filtering, length differentiation, tail behavior)\\n- [x] AI-assisted (OpenClaw agents 李飞飞/陈皮皮/毛豆豆, cross-reviewed, fully tested)\\n\\n## Backward compatibility\\n- `memoryFlushContextHash` undefined → falls back to existing `compactionCount` logic\\n- `memoryFlushCompactionCount` field preserved (not removed)\\n- First flush after upgrade runs normally (hash is empty = allow), subsequent flushes use hash On every subsequent request `resolveSessionModelRef` would return the fallback model, so the configured primary was **never retried** after it recovered.\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\n`updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun` unconditionally calls `setSessionRuntimeModel(next, { provider: providerUsed, model: modelUsed })` after every run. When a fallback ran, `providerUsed`/`modelUsed` reflect the fallback, and this gets written to `entry.model` / `entry.modelProvider`. `resolveSessionModelRef` then returns the stored runtime model on every future call, bypassing the configured primary entirely.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nAdd an `isFromFallback` parameter to `updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun`. When true, skip `setSessionRuntimeModel` so the session entry retains no runtime model (or retains its previous primary if one was stored). On the next request the session has no stale fallback recorded, so `resolveSessionModelRef` returns the configured primary and it gets a fresh retry.\\n\\nThe same guard is applied in the cron/isolated-agent path, which calls `setSessionRuntimeModel` directly.\\n\\nThe `isFromFallback` flag is computed at the agent.ts callsite as:\\n```ts\\nisFromFallback: fallbackModel !== model || fallbackProvider !== provider\\n```\\n\\n## What this does NOT change\\n\\n- Context token tracking still uses the actual model that ran (correct for prompt sizing)\\n- CLI session ID recording is unaffected\\n- The fallback model is still used for the current run — only the persistence step is skipped\\n- No change to `resolveSessionModelRef` itself\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\nExisting unit tests pass. Force a cache-bypassing re-read of `sessions.json` (handles the case where the store was written but the in-memory cache is stale)\\n2. If exactly one candidate is found, read its `{type:\\u0026#39;session\\u0026#39;}` header to extract the `sessionId`, then write a minimal synthetic store entry: `{ sessionId, updatedAt, sessionFile, spawnedBy, spawnDepth: 1 }`\\n\\nThis prevents false `\\u0026#39;missing-session-entry\\u0026#39;` orphan conclusions for the ~400ms race window between spawn and first store write.\\n\\n### Change 2: `resolveSubagentRunResumability()` — `subagent-resume.ts`\\n\\nReplaces the binary orphan/no-orphan check with a **4-way classification**:\\n\\n| State | Condition | Recovery action |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| `resumable-announce-only` | `endedAt` is already set | Retry announce delivery (already handled) |\\n| `resumable-replay` | Session-store entry exists, transcript has ≥1 assistant turn, no `endedAt` | Capture result from transcript, call `completeSubagentRun` |\\n| `resumable-fresh` | Session-store entry exists, transcript is empty/header-only, no `endedAt` | Re-dispatch original task via `callGateway(\\u0026#39;agent\\u0026#39;)` |\\n| `orphaned` | No session-store entry AND no recoverable transcript | Existing orphan-pruning behaviour |\\n\\n### Change 3: `resumeSubagentRun()` routing — `subagent-registry.ts`\\n\\nModified to call `routeResumedRun()` (which calls `resolveSubagentRunResumability()`) before falling through to the default `waitForSubagentCompletion` path:\\n\\n- **`resumable-replay`**: calls `completeSubagentRun` directly with `{ status: \\u0026#39;ok\\u0026#39; }`, which uses the existing `freezeRunResultAtCompletion` → `captureSubagentCompletionReply` flow to read the transcript result and trigger the announce flow. added an optional `runtimeContext` field to `ContextEngine.assemble()`\\n  - passed runtime prompt budget signals from the embedded runner into `assemble()`\\n  - preserved legacy compatibility for engines that reject unknown fields like `runtimeContext`\\n  - Any OS. Any Platform. The lobster way. 🦞 \"}},\"created_at\":\"2026-03-20T19:24:05Z\",\"updated_at\":\"2026-03-21T18:45:29Z\",\"closed_at\":\"2026-03-21T18:45:17Z\"},{\"number\":34222,\"title\":\"fix: use content hash for memory flush dedup instead of compactionCount (#30115)\",\"body\":\"## What\\nReplace event-based memory flush deduplication (`compactionCount`) with state-based deduplication (content hash) to prevent duplicate MEMORY.md writes when compaction aborts.\\n\\n## Why\\nFixes #30115 — Compaction abort triggers duplicate memory flushes in MEMORY.md.\\n\\nThe existing dedup uses `compactionCount` (an event counter) to decide whether to skip a flush. When compaction aborts and retries, the counter increments but the session context stays the same, causing the same content to be flushed repeatedly (4-7x duplicate entries reported).\\n\\nRoot cause: `compactionCount` conflates \\u0026#34;compaction cycle count\\u0026#34; with \\u0026#34;content has changed\\u0026#34; — these are independent concerns. Two different compaction cycles can see identical context (abort → retry scenario), so event-based dedup is fundamentally wrong for this use case.\\n\\n## How\\n- **State-based dedup**: compute a SHA-256 hash (truncated to 16 hex chars) of `messages.length + last 3 user/assistant message contents` before each flush. If the hash matches the stored `memoryFlushContextHash`, skip the flush.\\n- **Two-layer design**: `shouldRunMemoryFlush()` unchanged (token threshold gate), hash check added as second gate in `runMemoryFlushIfNeeded()`.\\n- **`willRetry` fix**: `onAgentEvent` now checks `!evt.data?.willRetry` before marking `memoryCompactionCompleted = true`, preventing retry-in-progress compaction from being incorrectly treated as completed.\\n- **Performance**: `readTranscriptTailMessages()` reads only the last 64KB of the transcript file (not the full file).\\n- **Hash timing**: stores the hash computed *before* the flush run (not after), since the flush turn itself writes to the transcript and would change the hash.\\n\\n### Scenario behavior\\n| Scenario | Behavior |\\n|----------|----------|\\n| Compaction abort | messages unchanged → hash unchanged → skip ✅ |\\n| Compaction success | messages compressed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| New messages | tail content changed → hash changed → allow flush ✅ |\\n| Persistence failure | `contextHashBeforeFlush` used in-memory → no re-flush within session ✅ |\\n\\n## Files changed (3 + 1 test)\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.ts` — new `computeContextHash()` function\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/agent-runner-memory.ts` — hash check gate + willRetry fix + tail reader\\n- `src/config/sessions/types.ts` — add `memoryFlushContextHash` field to `SessionEntry`\\n- `src/auto-reply/reply/memory-flush.test.ts` — 8 unit tests for `computeContextHash`\\n\\n## Testing\\n- [x] `pnpm build` passes\\n- [x] `pnpm check` passes (lint + format)\\n- [x] `pnpm test` — 811/812 pass (1 pre-existing failure in `process-respawn.test.ts`)\\n- [x] 8 new unit tests for `computeContextHash` (empty input, object content, undefined content, system message filtering, length differentiation, tail behavior)\\n- [x] AI-assisted (OpenClaw agents 李飞飞/陈皮皮/毛豆豆, cross-reviewed, On every subsequent request `resolveSessionModelRef` would return the fallback model, so the configured primary was **never retried** after it recovered.\\n\\n## Root cause\\n\\n`updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun` unconditionally calls `setSessionRuntimeModel(next, { provider: providerUsed, model: modelUsed })` after every run. When a fallback ran, `providerUsed`/`modelUsed` reflect the fallback, and this gets written to `entry.model` / `entry.modelProvider`. `resolveSessionModelRef` then returns the stored runtime model on every future call, bypassing the configured primary entirely.\\n\\n## Fix\\n\\nAdd an `isFromFallback` parameter to `updateSessionStoreAfterAgentRun`. When true, skip `setSessionRuntimeModel` so the session entry retains no runtime model (or retains its previous primary if one was stored). On the next request the session has no stale fallback recorded, so `resolveSessionModelRef` returns the configured primary and it gets a fresh retry.\\n\\nThe same guard is applied in the cron/isolated-agent path, which calls `setSessionRuntimeModel` directly.\\n\\nThe `isFromFallback` flag is computed at the agent.ts callsite as:\\n```ts\\nisFromFallback: fallbackModel !== model || fallbackProvider !== provider\\n```\\n\\n## What this does NOT change\\n\\n- Context token tracking still uses the actual model that ran (correct for prompt sizing)\\n- CLI session ID recording is unaffected\\n- The fallback model is still used for the current run — only the persistence step is skipped\\n- No change to `resolveSessionModelRef` itself\\n\\n## Testing\\n\\nExisting unit tests pass. The session store (`sessions.json`) survives on disk, but `waitForSubagentCompletion` → `agent.wait` RPC fails silently (or returns a spurious `\\u0026#39;timeout\\u0026#39;` status) because the agent process is gone — causing a false failure cascade. Runs that actually completed never deliver their results.\\n\\n## What this PR does (Phase 1)\\n\\nThree targeted changes in `src/agents/`:\\n\\n### Change 1: `rehydrateSessionStoreEntries()` — `subagent-resume.ts`\\n\\nCalled in `restoreSubagentRunsOnce()` **before** `reconcileOrphanedRestoredRuns()` so the orphan check sees a populated store entry.\\n\\nFor in-flight registry entries whose session-store entry is missing:\\n1. Force a cache-bypassing re-read of `sessions.json` (handles the case where the store was written but the in-memory cache is stale)\\n2. If still missing, scan the agent\\u0026#39;s sessions directory for a `.jsonl` transcript created within 5 minutes of the registry entry\\u0026#39;s `createdAt`\\n3. If exactly one candidate is found, read its `{type:\\u0026#39;session\\u0026#39;}` header to extract the `sessionId`, then write a minimal synthetic store entry: `{ sessionId, updatedAt, sessionFile, spawnedBy, spawnDepth: 1 }`\\n\\nThis prevents false `\\u0026#39;missing-session-entry\\u0026#39;` orphan conclusions for the ~400ms race window between spawn and first store write.\\n\\n### Change 2: `resolveSubagentRunResumability()` — `subagent-resume.ts`\\n\\nReplaces the binary orphan/no-orphan check with a **4-way classification**:\\n\\n| State | Condition | Recovery action |\\n|---|---|---|\\n| `resumable-announce-only` | `endedAt` is already set | Retry announce delivery (already handled) |\\n| `resumable-replay` | Session-store entry exists, transcript has ≥1 assistant turn, no `endedAt` | Capture result from transcript, call `completeSubagentRun` |\\n| `resumable-fresh` | Session-store entry exists, transcript is empty/header-only, no `endedAt` | Re-dispatch original task via `callGateway(\\u0026#39;agent\\u0026#39;)` |\\n| `orphaned` | No session-store entry AND no recoverable transcript | Existing orphan-pruning behaviour |\\n\\n### Change 3: `resumeSubagentRun()` routing — `subagent-registry.ts`\\n\\nModified to call `routeResumedRun()` (which calls `resolveSubagentRunResumability()`) before falling through to the default `waitForSubagentCompletion` path:\\n\\n- **`resumable-replay`**: calls `completeSubagentRun` directly with `{ status: \\u0026#39;ok\\u0026#39; }`, which uses the existing `freezeRunResultAtCompletion` → `captureSubagentCompletionReply` flow to read the transcript result and trigger the announce flow. No `agent.wait` call needed.\\n- **`resumable-fresh`**: re-dispatches the original task to the child session via `callGateway(\\u0026#39;agent\\u0026#39;)` (new idempotency key), waits with `agent.wait` on the **new** run ID, then calls `completeSubagentRun` for the **original** run entry.\\n- **`orphaned`** / **`resumable-announce-only`**: unchanged — routed by existing logic.\\n\\n## What Phase 2 will cover (not in this PR)\\n\\n- Synthetic `tool_result` injection for partially-completed transcripts (to avoid re-running from scratch when the agent was mid-tool-call)\\n- `SIGTERM` checkpointing to write a graceful shutdown marker to the transcript\\n- Per-run max-resume caps to prevent infinite retry loops on pathological transcripts\\n\\n## Tests\\n\\n25 new unit tests in `src/agents/subagent-resume.test.ts`:\\n- `readTranscriptSessionId` — 5 cases (valid header, missing file, wrong type, empty, malformed JSON)\\n- `transcriptHasAssistantTurn` — 6 cases (has assistant, header only, user only, missing, empty, malformed + valid)\\n- `resolveSubagentRunResumability` — 7 cases covering all 4 classifications\\n- `rehydrateSessionStoreEntries` — skip completed, skip existing, synthesise from transcript\\n- `routeResumedRun` — orphaned → false, announce-only → false, replay → true, fresh → true\\n\\n## References\\n\\nCloses #27875\\nRelated: #19780, #20436\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/43497\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"amittell\",\"id\":1388680,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/amittell\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/1388680?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"agents\",\"size: XL\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"feat/subagent-restart-resume-phase1\",\"sha\":\"264e3909462e062fbe001ba652ff095e33595423\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"amittell/openclaw\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant.
